  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5155957c-739e-4309-b4ed-8348a8359c8e'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7287408272342336406">A spellbinding, beautifully written novel that moves between contemporary times and one of the most fascinating and disturbing periods in American history--the Salem witch trials.<br/><br/>Harvard graduate student Connie Goodwin needs to spend her summer doing research for her doctoral dissertation. But when her mother asks her to handle the sale of Connie's grandmother's abandoned </span>
  <span id="freeText7287408272342336406" style="display:none">A spellbinding, beautifully written novel that moves between contemporary times and one of the most fascinating and disturbing periods in American history--the Salem witch trials.<br /><br />Harvard graduate student Connie Goodwin needs to spend her summer doing research for her doctoral dissertation. But when her mother asks her to handle the sale of Connie's grandmother's abandoned home near Salem, she can't refuse. As she is drawn deeper into the mysteries of the family house, Connie discovers an ancient key within a seventeenth-century Bible. The key contains a yellowing fragment of parchment with a name written upon it: Deliverance Dane. This discovery launches Connie on a quest--to find out who this woman was and to unearth a rare artifact of singular power: a physick book, its pages a secret repository for lost knowledge.<br /><br />As the pieces of Deliverance's harrowing story begin to fall into place, Connie is haunted by visions of the long-ago witch trials, and she begins to fear that she is more tied to Salem's dark past then she could have ever imagined.<br /><br />Written with astonishing conviction and grace, The Physick Book of Deliverance Dane travels seamlessly between the witch trials of the 1690s and a modern woman's story of mystery, intrigue, and revelation.<br />(katherinehowe.com)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7287408272342336406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/361720-just-wondering-if-this-is-age-appropriate">Just wondering if this is age appropriate for 5th grade? I&#39;m looking for a road trip book and I am too lazy to read it before we borrow it on audio.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_361720'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F4836308-the-physick-book-of-deliverance-dane">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/86057921-allison-fullen"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1567919814i/86057921._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/86057921-allison-fullen">Allison Fullen</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The first answer is exactly why young people need to read books like this. More concern about cursing and the mention of a natural part of a woman’s b<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The first answer is exactly why young people need to read books like this. More concern about cursing and the mention of a natural part of a woman’s body (they don’t even SAY the word clitoris, oh the pearl clutching! S/) than the murder and torture of innocent women. Sex is barely alluded to as a part of the story of the heroine’s falling in love. While this book is fiction, it can open discussion about real history, oppression and religion. THAT subject matter may be too mature for a 10 year old, but, maybe not. At this point in school, they are learning about war, kingdoms, dictatorship, and all of the related horrors. If there is more concern about anatomy, love making (not even described in this book) and words, but not the horrors inflicted on the women in this book (also not fully described), then YOU are the problem. <br /><br />Update: I wasn’t quite finished with the book when I wrote this, my mistake. They do describe the murders, with enough detail that even I, a 39 year old woman, was disturbed. I skipped some of it, it was so sad and infuriating. I can’t say I would recommend it for my kids at that age, but again, I’d rather they read curse words and about love and sex than the horrors of war and witches. We are more scared of mention of a girl’s clit than murder 🙄<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_183').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_111029483" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111029483" />
    <a title="Mary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2862333-mary"><img alt="Mary" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111029483?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary" href="/user/show/2862333-mary">Mary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111029483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3672655217128655149">I'VE GOT A PROBLEM WITH THIS BOOK ALREADY!!!<br/><br/>Only a few chapters into the book I am shocked at the following glaring error (and I hope there aren't any more of this magnitude before I'm done):<br/><br/>On page 35 when Liz asks Connie, "Did you ever meet her (Granna)?", Connie answers that her mother told her that she met her grandmother when she came to visit them in Concord. When Liz asks, "Do you remember any of this?", Connie says, "Not really. I think maybe I remember her dying.....I must have been abo</span>
  <span id="freeText3672655217128655149" style="display:none">I'VE GOT A PROBLEM WITH THIS BOOK ALREADY!!!<br /><br />Only a few chapters into the book I am shocked at the following glaring error (and I hope there aren't any more of this magnitude before I'm done):<br /><br />On page 35 when Liz asks Connie, "Did you ever meet her (Granna)?", Connie answers that her mother told her that she met her grandmother when she came to visit them in Concord. When Liz asks, "Do you remember any of this?", Connie says, "Not really. I think maybe I remember her dying.....I must have been about three or four."<br /><br />Then on page 44 it describes the "only Christmas with Granna that Connie could remember" when her grandmother brought hand knit sweaters that didn't fit right and Connie "chuckled with affection at the memory". Besides the fact that Connie already said she didn't remember her Granna, I also don't think a 3 or 4 year old child would comprehend the situation well enough to "chuckle at the memory" 20 years later.<br /><br />Seriously, this is a real problem for me. Even if the author was this careless in the continuity of the story, its hard to believe that it was never caught in editing. <br /><br />UPDATE (more than half way through the book)<br />Connie is flat out dumb! She supposedly has a masters degree in Colonial History yet she didn't know that "receipt" means "recipe" in that time period. She acts as though she never heard names like Patience and Prudence, which were common in the time period that she has supposedly studied for years. The moment when she figures out that Mercy and Marcy are the same name (just add the Brahmin accent and spell it like it sounds) is nothing short of DUHHHHH. She reads Prudence's journal which talks about going to deliver the neighbors' babies. A few hours later she has a eureka moment when she realizes that, hey, Prudence was a midwife! Puzzling over directions to put something in a "witch bottel", Connie scratches her head in bewilderment until she figures out that "bottel" must be the phonetic spelling of "bottle" therefore it must be "witch bottle". (Good thing the author spelled it out for those of us who might not have made that connection.) These are just a few examples of what a dim bulb Connie is although she is supposedly a PhD candidate. It is difficult to warm up to a main character who is such a poseur - in this case as an intellectual.<br /><br />UPDATE: (finished)<br />I wanted to like it, if only because of the subject matter and the great cover art. This is a book I might have read when I was 14 and loved it. But I take a huge exception with the review excerpt that compares this book to The Historian by Elizabeth Kostova. This book is written on a 7th grade reading level compared to Kostova's rich, layered, deeply woven tapestry of vampire lore. It is like comparing a Harlequin Romance to Gone With the Wind because they both take place in the South. <br /><br />The best parts of the book were the finely detailed scenes of daily life in the flashback chapters. The author has done a great job illustrating the speech patterns, behaviors, beliefs and habits of 18th century New Englanders. The book would have been so much better if she had focused more on that part of the story where she really shines. The modern day story was so trite and repetitious (how many times does Connie say, "Mom...." in an exasperated tone of voice?) that it diluted the impact of the riveting historical narrative.<br /><br />The over the top ending did nothing to redeem the story. It had a cartoonish quality that, again, would have been much more suitable in a book for young readers than a novel that aspires to be taken the least bit seriously. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3672655217128655149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanette (Again)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanette (Again)" href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-again">Jeanette (Again)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like irrelevant details</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=started-it-hated-it">started-it-hated-it</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61266331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16959478744751777661">If you're eagerly looking forward to reading this book, avoid my scathing review. <br/><br/>Sorry folks, if this review seems unkind, but I've got major hater tots for this book. I'm not averse to great detail if it's germane to the story or at least interesting, amusing, or informative. But must Ms. Howe describe for us each and every slant of light that passes through every window, and the piece of furniture or floor on which that slant of light falls? And the facial expression of every character in the</span>
  <span id="freeText16959478744751777661" style="display:none">If you're eagerly looking forward to reading this book, avoid my scathing review. <br /><br />Sorry folks, if this review seems unkind, but I've got major hater tots for this book. I'm not averse to great detail if it's germane to the story or at least interesting, amusing, or informative. But must Ms. Howe describe for us each and every slant of light that passes through every window, and the piece of furniture or floor on which that slant of light falls? And the facial expression of every character in the room and precisely how they sit or fold their hands? <br /><br />Trying to read this book was like having Katherine Howe jumping up and down in front of me waving her arms and saying, "SEE?!! See how GOOD I am at describing stuff?! SEE?!!" Yes, I see that you possess descriptive abilities, abilities much better suited to technical writing than to novels.<br /><br />Remember that old story about the optimist digging through a pile of manure saying, "There's got to be a pony in here somewhere!"? Well, there may be a story somewhere in this book, but I wasn't interested in digging through all the manure to uncover it. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17407230545750453174">I only rated this as high as I did because I thought the idea was really interesting but honestly the execution was terrible. The main character was so boring and flat and every time she had a thought I wanted to smash my head into the wall.   <span id="freeText17407230545750453174" style="display:none">I only rated this as high as I did because I thought the idea was really interesting but honestly the execution was terrible. The main character was so boring and flat and every time she had a thought I wanted to smash my head into the wall. The professor over seeing her dissertation was a creep, and her mother didn't appeal to me at all either. The writing was so slow and I really had to force myself to finish this one. Also it really stretched my suspension of disbelief especially believing that the main character is supposed to be intelligent like yeah okay. I'm so bored of skinny attractive smart girls who are insecure but still persevere. It was also pretty convenient how she met that hot guy who just happens to ends up helping her out with her mystery. I really wish I could get a refund for the time I spent making myself finish reading this.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2304836990" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2304836990" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63168028-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516912354p2/63168028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2304836990?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/63168028-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2304836990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15264426801900122246"><b>Witchcraft</b><br/>I loved the concept of a spellbook being uncovered in modern times with flashbacks to the Salem Witch trials of 1692. There is intrigue. Add a little bit of a thriller that other more sinister people want the book and you've got a cracker of a plot and an adventure story. Finally, add a great main character that you can trust to deliver the story, and surely a winner.<br/><br/>The problem is that the character, Connie, and the logic she applies doesn't match the supposed intelligence and qualifi</span>
  <span id="freeText15264426801900122246" style="display:none"><b>Witchcraft</b><br />I loved the concept of a spellbook being uncovered in modern times with flashbacks to the Salem Witch trials of 1692. There is intrigue. Add a little bit of a thriller that other more sinister people want the book and you've got a cracker of a plot and an adventure story. Finally, add a great main character that you can trust to deliver the story, and surely a winner.<br /><br />The problem is that the character, Connie, and the logic she applies doesn't match the supposed intelligence and qualifications she has from Harvard. She's a bit dumb - actually she's frustratingly dumb. It was also difficult to develop any empathy for Connie, which should have been a given, considering she should have been dealing with a personal historical weight on her shoulders. <br /><br />There is an interesting link, however, through the 2 time periods not only to add intrigue to the narrative but on another level to suggest what constrained social thinking between 1692 and nowadays, is completely different from a spiritual, social, moral and legal perspective.<br /><br />There are lots of plot holes and it lacked passion. It's a bit difficult when as a reader you're urging the author to do things to the story to make it more believable and entertaining, and they don't happen.<br /><br />It's difficult to heartily recommend this book as I would rate it 2.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15264426801900122246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_228287357" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228287357" />
    <a title="Richard Derus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus"><img alt="Richard Derus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494992210p2/3920693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228287357?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Derus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Derus" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228287357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer977067400749720888">Rating: 3.9* of five<br/><br/><b>The Publisher Says</b>: A spellbinding, beautifully written novel that moves between contemporary times and one of the most fascinating and disturbing periods in American history-the Salem witch trials.<br/><br/>Harvard graduate student Connie Goodwin needs to spend her summer doing research for her doctoral dissertation. But when her mother asks her to handle the sale of Connie's grandmother's abandoned home near Salem, she can't refuse. As she is drawn deeper into the mysteries of the fa</span>
  <span id="freeText977067400749720888" style="display:none">Rating: 3.9* of five<br><br><b>The Publisher Says</b>: A spellbinding, beautifully written novel that moves between contemporary times and one of the most fascinating and disturbing periods in American history-the Salem witch trials.<br><br>Harvard graduate student Connie Goodwin needs to spend her summer doing research for her doctoral dissertation. But when her mother asks her to handle the sale of Connie's grandmother's abandoned home near Salem, she can't refuse. As she is drawn deeper into the mysteries of the family house, Connie discovers an ancient key within a seventeenth-century Bible. The key contains a yellowing fragment of parchment with a name written upon it: Deliverance Dane. This discovery launches Connie on a quest--to find out who this woman was and to unearth a rare artifact of singular power: a physick book, its pages a secret repository for lost knowledge.<br><br>As the pieces of Deliverance's harrowing story begin to fall into place, Connie is haunted by visions of the long-ago witch trials, and she begins to fear that she is more tied to Salem's dark past then she could have ever imagined.<br><br>Written with astonishing conviction and grace, <i>The Physick Book of Deliverance Dane</i> travels seamlessly between the witch trials of the 1690s and a modern woman's story of mystery, intrigue, and revelation.<br><br><b>My Review</b>: This pretty-looking book was urged upon me by a fellow bookaholic whose previous urged reading, <i>The Hummingbird's Daughter</i>, was so ghastly and generally unpleasant to read that I was worried this book would be a stinker too. After all, hype + feminism + supernatural goins-on = *groan* for the typical Y-chromosome bearer.<br><br>I was completely wrong. I'm sorry I waited to read it.<br><br>Don't mistake me, it's a first novel with first-novel flaws, but it's a very good read and it's a promising debut. The basic story, a grad student in American History's discovery of a previously unknown primary source for data on the Salem witch trials, is built to excite the historian in me. The book itself, being a recipes-and-remedies book written by multiple generations of gifted women, also hooks my attention immediately.<br><br>The author, who is descended from an accused witch from Salem and who counts another, who died there, among her connections, is uniquely placed to make this story exciting. She is also a grad student, and she's made of storytelling stuff. No one who comes from such a lineage could escape the desire to make use of such great material. Considering the number of books, fiction and non, published about Salem, not many have tried. But Howe makes us invest in so much more than just the Salem-ness of the tale. She brings her creations to a simmer early in the book, and then lets 'em fly on the boil with a finely adjusted sense of pacing that I wish she'd teach to other novelists.<br><br>The first-novel blues come when Howe writes about her male characters. They're not well drawn, and their actions aren't very believeable. She also has some data withheld from her main character that I simply can't believe a mother would fail to mention to a daughter. (So as to avoid spoilers, I can't say what, but it's a pretty big omission IMHO.)<br><br>Hey, pobody's nerfect, right? I forgive these flaws because the story is so tightly paced, and so much of the time is spent with delightful characters, that it's an overall joy to read. Buy it new, in paperback, and you'll a) love the object itself since the publisher made a beautiful book, and b) support an author whose future work bids fair to make your dollars well spent. Very much recommended.<br><br><a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/deed.en_US" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="Creative Commons License" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380148217i/680962.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This work is licensed under a <a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/deed.en_US" rel="nofollow noopener">Creative Commons Attribution-NonCommercial-ShareAlike 3.0 Unported License</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="977067400749720888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_50541764" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50541764?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/1976749-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1976749-cheryl?shelf=review-gr">review-gr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1976749-cheryl?shelf=first-read-arc-giveaway">first-read-arc-giveaway</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50541764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12737216129700161660">There was so much that led me to believe I would thoroughly love this book. The topic is of interest to me on lots of levels (I too am related to many of the individuals on both sides of the Salem trials), I've visited the area before, the author has great credentials and has been educated at outstanding schools, the cover is beautiful, the publisher is pouring out a great deal of money into hype, and I enjoy historical fiction as well as looking at something from a different angle. I so looked </span>
  <span id="freeText12737216129700161660" style="display:none">There was so much that led me to believe I would thoroughly love this book. The topic is of interest to me on lots of levels (I too am related to many of the individuals on both sides of the Salem trials), I've visited the area before, the author has great credentials and has been educated at outstanding schools, the cover is beautiful, the publisher is pouring out a great deal of money into hype, and I enjoy historical fiction as well as looking at something from a different angle. I so looked forward to receiving my copy and when it arrived, I was delighted with the beautiful cover and feel of the book. I began to read it right away.<br /><br />Yet it fell totally flat and I was very disappointed. The story is stretched beyond the breaking point into silliness. This pseudo-memoir of the author's journey through the education system was full of stereotypes galore. In my opinion, the author perpetuates misconceptions and misinformation, not only about those innocent victims of hysteria but about the education system, Wicca, abilities that transcend current science, and people in general. In many ways, I was disappointed and vaguely offended with what felt like disrespect to my own intelligence as a reader. <br /><br />This book's hype probably contributed a great deal to my disappointment. If all I expected was a light read after a long day, this probably would have been ok. But I expected a lot better. Fortunately for the author, others like this book and will encourage others to buy it.<br /><br />•In compliance with FTC guidelines, received the book for free through Barnes &amp; Noble's First Reads. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_64928964" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64928964" />
    <a title="Jessika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1166992-jessika"><img alt="Jessika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547989302p2/1166992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64928964?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessika" href="/user/show/1166992-jessika">Jessika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166992-jessika?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166992-jessika?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166992-jessika?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166992-jessika?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166992-jessika?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64928964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13273253562917996803">Usually I'm not the type of person to just randomly go out to Barnes and Noble and buy a book that I'm not sure I'll enjoy. Something about this book pulled me in, though, and it didn't let go of me until I finished it just now. <br/><br/>I loved this book. Katherine Howe weaves her story with the finesse of a practiced writer, not someone who's just published her first novel. There was something about her writing style that I just couldn't get enough of. It wasn't too simple, but it wasn't too difficult </span>
  <span id="freeText13273253562917996803" style="display:none">Usually I'm not the type of person to just randomly go out to Barnes and Noble and buy a book that I'm not sure I'll enjoy. Something about this book pulled me in, though, and it didn't let go of me until I finished it just now. <br /><br />I loved this book. Katherine Howe weaves her story with the finesse of a practiced writer, not someone who's just published her first novel. There was something about her writing style that I just couldn't get enough of. It wasn't too simple, but it wasn't too difficult either--just balanced enough so that I was sucked into the story. Her switch between Massachusetts in the early 1990s and Massachusetts in the 1690s was smooth and effortless. I enjoyed that it didn't feel like there were two separate stories going on; they were both so entwined that it seemed that each was affecting and influencing each other. Her characters were all very well-developed, and the history was clearly well-researched and accurate. There weren't any hanging plot lines, so it was nice to see a story nicely wrapped up while still allowing the reader to speculate on the future of the characters. <br /><br />I also loved how Katherine Howe wrote the character of Connie, as a fact-driven, meticulous grad student, because if she hadn't done Connie that way, the second part of the book would have been too unbelievable. That being said, I thought she wrote that wisely and believably. <br /><br />Like I mentioned earlier, I found that the historical parts of the book seemed very accurate, so I'd recommend this book to fans of historical fiction. <br /><br />The only minor thing that got to me about this book was that some of her vocabulary choices and some of the dialect of the 1600s were a little jarring. That being said, I suppose the dialect was true to its time and would only naturally come a little awkwardly to me. <br /><br />It was nice to be able to delve into the lives of some of those accused in Salem. I found this to be one of the most unique takes on the period, as well, i.e. what if we didn't have the hindsight that modern America does? What if witchcraft is as real a problem as the flu, especially in the days when modern medical answers weren't available? What if there were <i>real witches</i> and not just women who fell victim to being low on the social ladder or young girls who "ate moldy bread"?<br /><br />Overall, very nicely done. Added to my list of favorites! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13273253562917996803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_60637292" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60637292" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1646501-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316020688p2/1646501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60637292?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/1646501-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6525011-the-physick-book-of-deliverance-dane">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646501-cheryl?shelf=kindle-edition">kindle-edition</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60637292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6364716115698384284">First, I did like this book. It is a great summer beach book; BUT it was much, much lighter than I thought it was going to be and given the hype I had been hoping for much more. The juxtaposition of the historical story and the modern story were very well done and the characters were likable and well thought out. The relationships between the characters in each time period were very real and believable and the descriptions of historical Salem and Marblehead and the Salem Witch Trials were intere</span>
  <span id="freeText6364716115698384284" style="display:none">First, I did like this book. It is a great summer beach book; BUT it was much, much lighter than I thought it was going to be and given the hype I had been hoping for much more. The juxtaposition of the historical story and the modern story were very well done and the characters were likable and well thought out. The relationships between the characters in each time period were very real and believable and the descriptions of historical Salem and Marblehead and the Salem Witch Trials were interesting and added a necessary richness to the tale. <br /><br />Now, that said, perhaps I have read way too many mysteries and I'm just getting really, really good at figuring things out, but I'd figured out pretty much the entire story for the most part, before I hit the middle of the book. I thought that the main character of Connie Goodwin seemed a little dim-witted for a graduate student in history, missing many many obvious answers in materials she was researching for clues to her mystery. So many that I found this small piece highly irritating and it did detract from my enjoyment of the story. <br /><br />While it was a fun read, I think that overall this book would appeal more to younger readers (high school/college) rather than rabid fans of historical fiction/mysteries in the vein of David Liss, Iain Pears, Ariana Franklin, Margaret Lawrence and even the lighter stories by Tasha Alexander and Deanna Raybourn.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6364716115698384284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_59054851" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59054851" />
    <a title="K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/373260-k"><img alt="K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199392765p2/373260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/59054851?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K" href="/user/show/373260-k">K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/373260-k?shelf=hyped-disappointments">hyped-disappointments</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59054851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13047660027481426746">This has gotten a lot of buzz lately in the library world. Four librarians including myself had holds on it before it even arrived at the building.   <span id="freeText13047660027481426746" style="display:none">This has gotten a lot of buzz lately in the library world. <div id="review_206705765" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206705765" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2411388-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272561978p2/2411388.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206705765?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/2411388-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2411388-hannah?shelf=historicals">historicals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2411388-hannah?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer206705765&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206705765" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10287988856286247838"><b>Rating Clarification: 2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Author Katherine Howe's take on the Salem Witch trials of the 1690's features a little twist: her story imagines that one of the accused really <u>had</u> supernatural talents....<br/><br/>The story begins in 1681 when young healer Deliverance Dane visits the home of Peter Petford and attempts to help his ailing 5 year old daughter Martha.<br/><br/>Fast forward to 1991: Harvard University, where our main character Connie Goodwin is getting ready to answer some final questions in her qualifyi</span>
  <span id="freeText10287988856286247838" style="display:none"><b>Rating Clarification: 2.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Author Katherine Howe's take on the Salem Witch trials of the 1690's features a little twist: her story imagines that one of the accused really <u>had</u> supernatural talents....<br /><br />The story begins in 1681 when young healer Deliverance Dane visits the home of Peter Petford and attempts to help his ailing 5 year old daughter Martha.<br /><br />Fast forward to 1991: Harvard University, where our main character Connie Goodwin is getting ready to answer some final questions in her qualifying exam for PhD candidacy. She is hoping to pass the orals, and spend the upcoming summer preparing her thesis on some aspect of American colonial history. A detour in her well laid plans occurs when her hippy, new-agey mother asks her to travel to Marblehead, Mass. and prepare her deceased grandmother's old house for sale. The house hasn't been lived in for 20 years, and is filled to the brim with the accumlated trash/treasure of centuries. What Connie discovers when cleaning out her granna's house is the basis for this lackluster tale of magic, superstition, prejudice and greed.<br /><br />This book had all the potential to be a clear favorite with me. You've got your Salem Witch trials, you've got your old house filled with secrets, you've got a story imbued with hints of real magic and supernatural elements, you've got a young woman with links and connections to other women centuries past, and you've got your wee canny canine. What's not to love? Well, almost everything.<br /><br />I will say that I did enjoy Howe's story featuring Deliverance Dane and her life. These snippets occured sporatically throughout the book, and were interesting and entertaining. Had the entire book been about Deliverance, I would probably have given this book 4 stars or more. Unfortunately, the majority of the book focused on modern day Connie, surely one of the stupidest candidates for PhD candidacy that Harvard has <u>ever</u> considered. Connie, while touted by the writer as a brilliant and clever young mind destined for BIG things in the world of colonial academia, displayes mind boggling idiocy when it comes to the most simple observations on colonial life. She is amazed and stunned by phonetic spellings of colonial first names (i.e. Marcy = Mercy - SHAAAZAM, who'd have guessed?!?). Although she is a born and Massachusetts native, she continually marvels over the speach patterns displayed by Boston Brahmins and similar citizens of her native state. WTH? Umm, people generally notice variations in speech when they are <u>NOT</u> native to the area, but Connie apparently finds the style of speech of her people extraordinary. In fact, Connie is so incredibly dense <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ that <b><i>her very own</i></b> full name, "Constance", completely floors her with it's colonial associations. In point of fact, she even seems to forget that her name <i><b>is</b></i> Constance. Will somebody please explain to me how this is possible without amnesia or a full frontal lobotomy? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Connie is, IMO, so stupid, so uninspiring, so vapid a creature that it boggles the mind to think <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ she could ever share one atom of genetic material with the interesting Deliverance <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And as Connie's story makes up 90% of the book's plot, it makes for a very tedious and boring story. The wonder of it all is that I gave it 2.5 stars, but I did find parts of it very moving and page turning.<br /><br />This is one of those books, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2873264.The_Tenth_Gift" title="The Tenth Gift by Jane Johnson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tenth Gift</a>, that had great potential, but lacked skillful execution. There were flashes of it here and there, but not enough consistency to make it a winner in my mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10287988856286247838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_199889557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199889557" />
    <a title="Kenryth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5629898-kenryth"><img alt="Kenryth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507482886p2/5629898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199889557?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kenryth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kenryth" href="/user/show/5629898-kenryth">Kenryth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199889557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12839859988449443021">Very badly written "mystery" that manages to make the Salem era boring. The average reader picks up the clues entire chapters before Our Heroine, Connie, figures them out, and often has to stop reading long enough for her to catch up. I think this book was set in 1991 so that Connie would not have access to the Internet. A few hours on Google or Wikipedia might have solved the mystery in an afternoon. <br/><br/>As several other reviewers have pointed out, the heroine doesn't seem to possess enough brain m</span>
  <span id="freeText12839859988449443021" style="display:none">Very badly written "mystery" that manages to make the Salem era boring. The average reader picks up the clues entire chapters before Our Heroine, Connie, figures them out, and often has to stop reading long enough for her to catch up. I think this book was set in 1991 so that Connie would not have access to the Internet. A few hours on Google or Wikipedia might have solved the mystery in an afternoon. <br /><br />As several other reviewers have pointed out, the heroine doesn't seem to possess enough brain matter to complete a simple crossword puzzle, never mind work on her PhD while simultaneously solving a Big Mystery. Connie also has a house that doesn't decay through time or neglect, although I guess we could believe it has a handy magic spell protecting it from wood-rot, mice, and holes in the roof. And seriously, if you are on the hunt for a missing book, maybe you could explore the actual house where you found the big clue. <br /><br />And when Connie had the big revelation that her real name was Constance???? Did she really forget her own name? Considering that the main characters are called Deliverance, Mercy, Prudence and Grace, is it too much to ask that Connie picks up on the fact that her own biblically inspired moniker might be relevant?<br /><br />Plus, the author clearly has an issue with shop clerks and library staff; almost every single one is rude and unhelpful and makes Poor Connie do all the nasty grunt work herself.<br /><br />And if you want to write a story set in another era, feel free to sprinkle the dialogue with "thou" and "thee", but please refrain from using phonetic spellings of the local dialect.<br /><br />Thas booke maihde my heade hurte. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12839859988449443021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_50496819" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50496819" />
    <a title="Nely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1440151-nely"><img alt="Nely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271166357p2/1440151.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50496819?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nely" href="/user/show/1440151-nely">Nely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50496819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13508980039412711017">This is the story of Connie Goodwin, a doctoral candidate in American History at Harvard, who (upon her mother’s request) spends the summer cleaning and clearing out her grandmother's house that has been vacant for 20 years in Marblehead, Massachusetts. Little did Connie know what she was in store for when she agreed to this tedious task. <br/><br/>While browsing through her grandmother’s old books, Connie stumbles upon a very old key in a bible. Attached to this key is an equally old slip of paper with t</span>
  <span id="freeText13508980039412711017" style="display:none">This is the story of Connie Goodwin, a doctoral candidate in American History at Harvard, who (upon her mother’s request) spends the summer cleaning and clearing out her grandmother's house that has been vacant for 20 years in Marblehead, Massachusetts. Little did Connie know what she was in store for when she agreed to this tedious task. <br /><br />While browsing through her grandmother’s old books, Connie stumbles upon a very old key in a bible. Attached to this key is an equally old slip of paper with the name, Deliverance Dane. <br /><br />Told through flashbacks from Salem in the late 1690's we learn the story of Deliverance, a woman condemned as a witch in 1692, her daughter and eventually her granddaughter, as well as the history of the "Receipt Book" which is handed down from generation to generation.<br /><br />As Connie tries to get the house back to rights in order to sell it for lack of payment of taxes, she is also working on her doctorate course and is persuaded by her adviser to find Deliverance's physick book otherwise known as a Shadow Book which might be the perfect topic for her doctorate - having found an unknown Salem witch. <br /><br />I could not put this down! -- this is historical fiction at it's finest. It makes you want to know more about the time and immerses you wholly in it's world. The link in the story between contemporary times and the past is gripping as well as the commentary on religion and the Salem Witch Trials. I especially liked that Ms. Crouch uses so much detail when describing Salem in 1692. The houses, the way they talked, dressed, lived was all very detailed. She uses real names and events to depict Deliverance’s demise. She definitely did her research and it was neat to read that she was related to two of the named witches. I highly recommend this.<br /><br />This book will be available in June, so make sure to make a note of it and put it on your TBR list so you don’t forget to pick up a copy. In my opinion, you will not be disappointed. I’m dying to see what the finished product will look like - since I only have an ARC. But the binding, with its flap covering the pages, beautiful artwork, and thick paper makes this book quite a treasure. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13508980039412711017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_73772996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73772996" />
    <a title="Wyndie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1690838-wyndie"><img alt="Wyndie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1227665686p2/1690838.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73772996?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wyndie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wyndie" href="/user/show/1690838-wyndie">Wyndie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73772996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3461190580521565692">Bravo to whoever was responsible for the book jacket. I was drawn in by a glowing review from Matthew Pearl, the author of “The Dante Club.” The premise looked like a unique spin to one of America’s more tragic parts of history, the Salem witch trials. However the novel was a poorly written 375 page disappointment. <br/><br/>I felt much like Connie; searching for a book. The characters (living and dead) were void of dimension, making it difficult for me to feel vested in her quest for Deliverance Dane. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText3461190580521565692" style="display:none">Bravo to whoever was responsible for the book jacket. I was drawn in by a glowing review from Matthew Pearl, the author of “The Dante Club.” The premise looked like a unique spin to one of America’s more tragic parts of history, the Salem witch trials. However the novel was a poorly written 375 page disappointment. <br /><br />I felt much like Connie; searching for a book. The characters (living and dead) were void of dimension, making it difficult for me to feel vested in her quest for Deliverance Dane. The modern portion of the tale was set in 1991. This reflects poorly on Howe’s ability as an author. Apart from one minor comment about the seemingly absurd use of a cell phone, there was not much else that grounded the reader in 1991. Her main character, Connie Goodwin uses pre Google research methods. A wild-goose chase for an allusive manuscript in 2009 would comprise of countless mind-numbing hours on the computer. I understand her need for Connie to search in card catalogues, and the ability to handle the actual books, it propels her through the plot. Howe should have wholeheartedly embraced 1991 time period with even half of the detail and accuracy as her tales of the 1690’s. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="3461190580521565692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_87462933" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87462933" />
    <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish"><img alt="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398981306p2/1113032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87462933?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=own-have-read">own-have-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=magic-spells-witchcraft-curses">magic-spells-witchcraft-curses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=pnr-contemporary">pnr-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=salem-witch-trials">salem-witch-trials</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=pnr-witches">pnr-witches</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87462933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8969779043469819057"><br/>For as long as I can remember, I’ve been fascinated with the Salem witch hunts. Even as a young girl in elementary school, I read books, watched movies and loved listening to stories about the witch trials and the events leading up to them. So when I saw <i> The Physick Book of Deliverance Dane</i>, it goes without saying that I just had to have it. <br/><br/>We first meet our heroine, Connie Goodwin, as she’s about to answer the final question in her qualifying exam at Harvard; <i> “Would you please provide the co</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8969779043469819057" style="display:none"><br />For as long as I can remember, I’ve been fascinated with the Salem witch hunts. Even as a young girl in elementary school, I read books, watched movies and loved listening to stories about the witch trials and the events leading up to them. So when I saw <i> The Physick Book of Deliverance Dane</i>, it goes without saying that I just had to have it. <br /><br />We first meet our heroine, Connie Goodwin, as she’s about to answer the final question in her qualifying exam at Harvard; <i> “Would you please provide the committee with a succinct and considered history of witchcraft in North America?”</i> Now, Connie is an incredibly intelligent woman, trying to impress a panel of equally intelligent – if not more so - Harvard professors with her knowledge of American Colonial history. The dialog and accompanying narrative reflected the importance of her answer, and for a brief time I found myself kind of lost in the “educated” explanation. However, once we get past that part in the story, which didn’t last very long, I easily fell into the flow and the feel of Katherine Howe’s writing. <br /><br />I’ve found that sometimes when an author tackles a fictional retelling of factual historical events, it can end up boring and text bookish for the reader. I think it takes skill to stay true to the details without putting the reader to sleep. Thankfully, Katherine Howe pulled this off beautifully.<br /><br />I was quickly pulled into the story and felt very much a part of Connie’s journey to find Deliverance Dane’s missing Physick Book. The glimpses into the past we were given as we moved between 1991 and the late 17th and early 18th centuries flowed very well, and I really feel like the author did a brilliant job of taking us from one time period to another, as we moved from chapter to chapter. <br /><br />Along the way, Connie meets Sam, and a romance develops between them. I really enjoyed that aspect of the story because Sam was a great character, but I wish we could have seen a little more relationship development between them, so that I could have felt the depth of her emotions for him during certain parts of the book. However, that said, I thought the author did an excellent job of making his a character someone I cared about even though we didn’t get to spend a whole lot of time with him. And a note for those who might be interested, while we know that Connie and Sam do have a sexual relationship, there was nothing sexually explicit in this book. <br /><br />Overall, this was a great story, with a fun twist, that I couldn’t put down. It had me imaging what it would be like if I had lived during this time period, and answered questions I’ve long had. And I even shed a few tears over what it must have been like for the families of the accused. <br /><br />I’d love to get my hands on something else along the lines of <i>The Physick Book of Deliverance Dane, </i>and will be keeping my eyes open for more by this author.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8969779043469819057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_101289994" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101289994" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1605591-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252166169p2/1605591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101289994?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/1605591-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781401341336" href="/book/show/6987086-the-physick-book-of-deliverance-dane">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=minority-and-women-writers">minority-and-women-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=historical-1700-1900">historical-1700-1900</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101289994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15685823728747494163">In the 90s, there was a series called <i>Poltergeist the Legacy</i>. It was about a group of people who investigated paranormal mysteries. It was kinda good. There was an episode that supposedly took place in Boston. The series supposedly took place in San Fran but considering that the money was always marked with Queen Elizabeth II's head, the series was mostly likely filmed in CA. Anyway, the Boston show was about a history grad student who discovers that her ancestor might have been a witch.<br/><br/>Go watch</span>
  <span id="freeText15685823728747494163" style="display:none">In the 90s, there was a series called <i>Poltergeist the Legacy</i>. It was about a group of people who investigated paranormal mysteries. It was kinda good. There was an episode that supposedly took place in Boston. The series supposedly took place in San Fran but considering that the money was always marked with Queen Elizabeth II's head, the series was mostly likely filmed in CA. Anyway, the Boston show was about a history grad student who discovers that her ancestor might have been a witch.<br /><br />Go watch that instead of trying to read this book. At the very least, you can drool over good looking people.<br /><br />I do not know how this got named one of the top ten books of 2009 as well as all the other endorsement blurbs on the cover. Maybe, newspapers and magazines should comission reviews by people who (a) actually read (b) actually read more than one fantasy novel per year or (c) have intelligence.<br /><br />The book sounds promising, if making use of an already used idea (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11359.Marion_Zimmer_Bradley" title="Marion Zimmer Bradley" rel="nofollow noopener">Marion Zimmer Bradley</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice" title="Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne Rice</a> have used similar ideas in thier witch books). The book fails, however, really, really fails. The first and major problem is Connie, a.k.a Mary Sue.<br /><br />Connie's problems include:<br /><br />1. She's smart and everyone else knows it but her.<br />2. She's skinny.<br />3. She doesn't sound like a dog owner.<br />4. She doesn't sound like a grad student because<br /> a. She doesn't have any basic research skills.<br /> b. She doesn't seem to have any knowledge of any language <br /> besides English.<br />5. She has a father who disappered (angst and sorrow!)<br />6. Her mother is a hippie who doesn't understand her and who doesn't act like an adult (poor baby!)<br />7. She can't really remember her Granna (shucks!)<br />8. Her advisor is a sexist dude. (Oh dear).<br /><br />Additionally, why does everyone in Boston who encounters Connie and who is not academic act rude? Honestly, if I were running an archive and some stupid bimbo showed up in cut offs and flip flops (but seemingly without a shirt, considering we are not told what that looks like), I might not be so willing to hand over the keys either.<br /><br />Then she meets her true love. Nice!<br /><br />Other problems include the fact that anyone can figure out who the bad guy is (watch out Nancy Drew) and too much telling and not enough showing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15685823728747494163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_968016673" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/968016673" />
    <a title="Tiffany PSquared" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27443399-tiffany-psquared"><img alt="Tiffany PSquared" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492731992p2/27443399.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/968016673?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiffany PSquared" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiffany PSquared" href="/user/show/27443399-tiffany-psquared">Tiffany PSquared</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27443399-tiffany-psquared?shelf=bookmooch-giveaways">bookmooch-giveaways</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27443399-tiffany-psquared?shelf=2017-book-reading-challenge">2017-book-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer968016673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16117904431524015433">❝<b>We can understand the world only through the language that is at our disposal. Every period has its own linguistic - and perceptive - lens.</b>❞<br/><br/>Historic and modern-day Massachusetts reunite in this tale of one woman's unintentional climb through her family tree. Connie discovers more than she bargains for while researching for her doctoral dissertation.<br/><br/><u>
  <b>What I Liked:</b>
</u><br/>- I have read several books about the Salem witch trials, but none that were based in modern times. This put the trials into a new </span>
  <span id="freeText16117904431524015433" style="display:none">❝<b>We can understand the world only through the language that is at our disposal. Every period has its own linguistic - and perceptive - lens.</b>❞<br><br>Historic and modern-day Massachusetts reunite in this tale of one woman's unintentional climb through her family tree. Connie discovers more than she bargains for while researching for her doctoral dissertation.<br><br><u>
  <b>What I Liked:</b>
</u><br>- I have read several books about the Salem witch trials, but none that were based in modern times. This put the trials into a new perspective and was, to me, an original take on that history.<br>- From the postscript, we learn that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/342135.Katherine_Howe" title="Katherine Howe" rel="nofollow noopener">Katherine Howe</a> herself can trace her lineage back to two accused witches. This fact lends an air of authority, truthfulness, and connectedness to the tale.<br>- I loved the Interludes where we popped back in time to revisit several members of the Dane family line as they practiced their craft, defended themselves, and made their living in their highly suspicious environment.<br>- The characters were fleshed out, the setting well-established, and the pacing was steady.<br>- The cover art pulled me in even before the story did.<br><br><u>
  <b>What I Didn't Like:</b>
</u><br>- Connie's mother, Grace, was intended to be mysterious, but maybe too much so. I felt sure that we would get more exposure to an explanation from her, but the book ended without that being the case.<br>- Once again - as often happens in suspenseful novels - the story ended without much follow-up after the resolution. I guess it may just be me, but with good books, I hate to let them end without knowing what happens with the main characters, their relationships, and their careers. I guess that's why I read so many series.<br><br>This was a well-paced, entertaining work of historical fiction written in a way that kept me hooked. Four well-earned stars.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1510502735i/24425843.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16117904431524015433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dfunky1" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dfunky1" href="/user/show/1168122-dfunky1">Dfunky1</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer64517175&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer64517175" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6990535242016128128">I really wanted to like this book as it's hard to find a novel that mixes historical elements and more contemporary ones, and the publicity for this novel suggested that Howe had been highly successful in doing so. <br/><br/>But what I found was that this book was uneven: the projections back into the colonial New England past were compelling; those to 1991-1992 were filled with one-dimensional characters, highly predicable events, ridiculous coincidences, and superficial glosses on everything from love t</span>
  <span id="freeText6990535242016128128" style="display:none">I really wanted to like this book as it's hard to find a novel that mixes historical elements and more contemporary ones, and the publicity for this novel suggested that Howe had been highly successful in doing so. <br /><br />But what I found was that this book was uneven: the projections back into the colonial New England past were compelling; those to 1991-1992 were filled with one-dimensional characters, highly predicable events, ridiculous coincidences, and superficial glosses on everything from love to history to the universe and its workings.<br /><br />I have to say--as an art historian whose area is ancient and, therefore, who often deals with precious and delicate materials--that the heroine's touching of one text with her bare hands and throwing of another one into a fire are unconscionable, even if fictional!<br /><br />Moreover, Howe wrote the "villain" as so caricatured from the outset that the reader was immediately clued in that this was not going to be suspenseful in any way. Finally, Howe's heroine "Connie" who supposedly had done better than almost anyone her committee had ever seen on her qualifying exams, was rather obtuse about every little aspect of the supposed mystery she was unraveling.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6990535242016128128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
